Nantong 86

Bandit Leader from Tongru Executed in Baipu: Feng Ziping, the bandit leader from Tongru, also known as Feng Chensi, was arrested in Baipu while disguised as a fisherman with 13 guns. He was sentenced to death by the county government. The bandit appealed to the province, and the provincial government ordered the county to investigate and report. The county government reviewed and reported the case of the Feng bandit, and on the 22nd, an electric order was received, approving the execution of Feng Ziping. County Magistrate Zhang escorted the bandit to Baipu for execution by shooting.

Rural Farmer Accidentally Detonates Hand Grenade, Causing Disaster: Zhang Cun, a rural farmer from Baitang Temple on Langshan Road, and his son Zhang Run, picked up an undetonated hand grenade from a military exercise and took it home. They wanted to remove the wooden handle. Zhang Cun's wife played with it and put it in the stove to burn. Suddenly, it exploded, collapsing the house. Zhang's wife's face was blurred, and she collapsed in a pool of blood. Zhang's father and son happened to be out and were not injured. Zhang's wife has been sent to the hospital for treatment and is in critical condition.

Department of Education Orders County to Recover Education Funds: The Nantong Education Depository Public Funds, which are paper money converted into silver dollars, are to be calculated at the price of foreign currency at the time of deposit, according to the interpretation of the Ministry of Justice and Administration. The pawnshop owners refused, and the county government reported to the Department of Education. On the 22nd, Director Zhou ordered the county to arrest and strictly pursue Yao Hanzai and others, the representatives of the pawnshop owners. County Magistrate Zhang immediately complied.

Chongming 87

Notorious Bandit Cao Aqing Arrested: The home of Zhang Sanjiang, a resident of the Fifth District of the county, was robbed by bandits last month in the middle of the night. He immediately reported to the county for arrest, and the land and water police departments repeatedly ordered the arrest, but no one was captured. Recently, Mao Xiaoshan, an investigator from the 17th Team of the Fourth District of the Provincial Public Security Team on the water, learned that the notorious bandit Cao Aqing was hiding in the Taizhou Stack in Lujiazui, Pudong. He secretly reported to Gong, the captain of the team, who carried official documents and went to Shanghai yesterday to request the assistance of the police from the Third Branch Bureau of the Shanghai Special City Public Security Bureau. The bandit Cao was captured on the spot and sent to the bureau. After a brief interrogation by the director of the bureau, the bandit confessed that he was 35 years old, from Chongming, and had no fixed address. The director of the bureau ordered that he be sent to the main bureau for interrogation and that the investigator prepare a document to transfer the case for trial.

Pinghu 88

Faji Steamer Robbed: The New Qingying, a steamer from the Faji Steamer Bureau, was fully loaded with watermelons yesterday and transported to Shanghai for sale. It returned to Pinghu on the same night. At around 8:40 PM, while passing through the Sanlintang Estuary, it encountered more than 30 bandits who blocked the road with a boat and fired several shots, ordering the ship to stop. The ship could not avoid them and had to submit to the robbery. It is estimated that more than 1,000 yuan in silver was robbed from the watermelon vendors and more than 200 yuan in silver from the ship's purser. The incident lasted 40 minutes before the bandits left. Afterwards, the boatmen reported to the Jiangsu Water Public Security Team, which sent warships to pursue them, but there was no trace of them.

Wounded Soldiers Pass Through and Beg: Eight wounded and disabled soldiers from the Third Division of the National Army, who had been wounded in the war of resistance against Japan, passed through the county yesterday from Hangzhou to Shanghai and begged along the way. Seeing that the shops were openly selling Japanese goods, they sighed and shed tears. Later, Zhu, the platoon leader of the Third Jia Platoon of the local Defense Corps, led them to the Chamber of Commerce, where each was given 5 jiao, which they thanked and left.

Huzhou 89

Silk Factories Temporarily Stop Weaving: Since the Shanghai Incident, transactions have been suspended at the silk weaving factories in the city, and the scarcity of silver has made it difficult to maintain operations. This spring, the owners of the factories had no intention of opening for business, but because the workers repeatedly requested to start weaving and were willing to reduce their wages, the factories勉强 opened for business to support the workers. Before long, the wages returned to their original state. Recently, due to the sharp drop in silk prices, the silk market has plummeted. The factories have a large stock of silk, and the losses are incalculable. Therefore, the manufacturers gathered at the Machine Industry Association the other day and resolved to temporarily stop weaving from yesterday (the 21st) until the market improves slightly, and then resume operations.

Residents of Panjiawan Robbed: Zhang Hanyun, 61, who lives in Panjiawan near the Guangling Temple in Shuanglin Town, is a bit wealthy. Unexpectedly, around 12:00 AM the other day, more than 20 bandits suddenly came, each holding a wooden-cased gun and speaking with a Henan accent. They broke into the house and robbed all the clothes, silk, and cash. After the robbery, the bandits went to the homes of Zhang Manzi and Zhang Meisheng and broke down the doors, robbing them at will, taking away all the clothes, quilts, silk, and cotton. It is now reported that the losses of the three families are about 1,000 yuan or more. Afterwards, the local township head Zhang reported to the Shuanglin Public Security Branch Bureau for pursuit.

Xiaoshan 90

Robbery Cases Repeatedly Occur in the Suburbs: In the Houwu area outside the South Gate of Xiaoshan, five bandits speaking with foreign accents suddenly came on the afternoon of the 19th and broke into the homes of the Wu and Yu families, robbing them wantonly. Then, because there were fishing boats racing on the riverbank, the bandits suspected something was wrong and fled towards the South Gate Port. After the inspection, clothes and silver coins worth more than 200 yuan were stolen. On the 20th, two cloth vendors along Xiang Lake were stopped and searched by five bandits in the Qingshan Zhang area, and a total of 10 yuan in silver, 5 yuan in paper money, and 20 jiao in small silver coins were robbed.

Fire in Xicheng Kills Two People: The home of Li Caibao, a resident of Dongsha Xicheng in Xiaoshan, caught fire on the night of the 19th when a lamp overturned a mosquito net, burning down three buildings and spreading to the homes of three neighbors, including the Zhang family. Li's young son, 10, and second son, 16, were unable to escape because the ladder had been broken when the fire started and died in the fire. The next morning, only their hearts and lungs were left in the fire pit, which was a tragic sight.

Two Silver Dollars Cost a Life: Xu Yousheng, a farmer from Gaodianshang outside the West Gate of Xiaoshan, was quite diligent and thrifty. This time, he was sick in bed and instructed his wife, Wang, to pawn his clothes in a pawnshop for two silver dollars to buy food and medicine. Unexpectedly, his wife had the silver coins snatched by a pickpocket on the way. Thinking that she could not go home to see her husband, she drowned herself in the Shanbei River. After passers-by tried their best to rescue her, she had already stopped breathing.Correction:In the Haifeng correspondence in the 17th edition of this newspaper, it was reported that the provincial accounting association sent personnel to thoroughly investigate the case. Important Education News

Summer Military Training is Imperative 91

The Ministry of Education Reissues Orders to Provincial and Municipal Education Departments and Bureaus to Implement Summer Military Training in Schools: The Ministry of Education, considering that summer military training in all schools is imperative, has reissued orders to provincial and municipal education departments and bureaus, stating: "It is approved that the Training Supervisory Department has consulted and opened, and it has been found that all high schools and above should implement summer military training this year in accordance with the regulations. Previously, we have telegraphed and ordered various education administrative agencies and schools to follow suit. Recently, according to reports from military instructors in various schools, many schools have reported their implementation in accordance with the regulations, but there are also many who have used the excuse that they have not received clear orders from your department and the relevant education departments, hoping to shirk their responsibility. Such disregard for the difficulties of the times and neglect of laws and regulations is inappropriate. It is appropriate to consult and strictly order various education administrative agencies and schools to implement this year's summer training in accordance with the regulations. For schools whose students have already started their summer vacation and cannot be gathered temporarily, training can be conducted three weeks before the start of the first semester of the 21st academic year. For those who have missed too many classes due to the invasion of Shanghai by the暴日 and need to make up other subjects, military training can be conducted for 12 hours per week, with one-half for academic subjects and two-thirds for technical subjects to take both into account, etc. With this approval, it is found that this year's summer military training has been implemented repeatedly by the ministry's orders and must be carried out. Schools at all levels, if they have already started their vacation and students cannot be gathered, should be allowed to conduct training three weeks before the start of the next academic year and should not use excuses to shirk their responsibility. In addition to separate orders, we urgently order you to forward this order to all public and private high schools and above under your jurisdiction to comply."

Shandong Education Discussion Meeting Concludes 94

Discussion on Teacher Training and Public Education

Jinan, 23rd: The education problem discussion meeting discussed teacher training on the 21st. As a result, kindergarten and rural teacher training courses were established in teacher training schools, teacher training classes were established, high school graduates were admitted, and graduates were produced in one year. Simple teacher training classes were set up in both middle school and teacher training schools, high school graduates were admitted, and graduates were produced in one year. Simple teacher training schools admitted elementary school graduates and graduated in four years. Teacher training schools should be set up in rural areas as a principle, and the equipment and methods should be aimed at creating a social center, and the internship methods should be improved to emphasize both teaching and learning. This afternoon, the education problem discussion meeting concluded after discussing vocational middle schools and public education. He Siyuan, representing the education community of the province, thanked the celebrities who attended the meeting. At noon, the provincial party department held a banquet at the Lixia Ning public banquet, and Li Zheng, Yang Lian, and Liu Tingfang returned to Ping at night.

Opening of the Provincial Shanghai Middle School Summer School 97

The fifth session of the Shanghai Middle School Summer School of Jiangsu Province opened at 8:00 AM yesterday in the auditorium of the junior high division. Over 800 guests, faculty, and students attended. After a group photograph, they entered the auditorium in orderly fashion, full of energy and solemnity. Summer School Director Shen Yizhen presided over the ceremony. Principal Zheng Xigu gave a speech, outlining the summer school's objectives: (1) to provide supplementary instruction in core subjects to prepare for further education; (2) to allow both the school and students to gain a deeper understanding of each other. He concluded by saying, "Since last year, China has been beset by natural and man-made disasters, internal and external troubles following one after another. We young people should make use of the summer vacation to study diligently, endure hardship, and prepare to wipe out national humiliation in the future." Next, Tongji University President Hu Shuhua gave a speech, encouraging students in the following aspects: (1) cherish time; (2) save the nation through science; (3) boycott enemy goods; (4) be honest, simple, and frugal; (5) oppose civil war; (6) develop the Northwest; (7) engage in air defense drills. He then introduced Summer School Dean Lu Shaoji, Guidance Director Wang Zongshi, and Administrative Director Wei Jiguang. Finally, Director Shen reported on school affairs, providing detailed guidance on all aspects of education, guidance, and administration. The meeting concluded at 11:00 AM.

The Situation After the Restoration of Lida Academy 98

The Lida Academy in Jiangwan suffered greatly when it fell into the war zone during the Japanese invasion of Shanghai. The breeding chicken farm near the racecourse was completely destroyed, and all school equipment was stolen. Later, when the 19th Route Army retreated to the second defense line, all equipment and agricultural products of the high school agricultural education department in Nantao Chaitang were also looted. The total direct losses suffered by the school in the Shanghai battle amounted to over 140,000 yuan. Fortunately, not many school buildings were destroyed, making repairs easier. After the end of the war in early May, the school's principals began the restoration work. With the support of school board members Li Shizeng, Wu Zhihui, and Yi Yincun, significant funds were raised to rebuild the school buildings and purchase school equipment at both the Jiangwan and Nantao locations. Approval was obtained from the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education to open a summer remedial class on July 1st to make up for the students' interrupted studies during the war, so that they could be promoted to the next grade as usual next semester. The initial restoration is nearing completion, with the school buildings and equipment presenting a brand new look. The spirit of teachers and students is very high. It is also reported that the school has purchased over 40 buildings on Lida Road in Yongyi Lane, preparing to expand enrollment and provide housing for faculty and staff families next semester.

White Goose Alumni to Hold Tea Party Today 99

The White Goose Painting Institute, a well-known art group formerly located on Changchun Road in North Sichuan Road, was severely affected by the January 28th Incident, as its location was in the war zone, resulting in the complete destruction of all its buildings and the dispersal of its students. Now, some students and the institute's founders, Chen Qiucao, Fang Xuegu, and Du Xueou, in order to promote communication and friendship among the students, have jointly initiated a tea party to be held this Sunday afternoon at 4:00 PM in the Guifei Hall on the second floor of the Guanshengyuan on Nanjing Road. All former students of White Goose are welcome to join.

China Youth Volleyball Tournament: Haige Wins Championship 100

Defeated Czechoslovakia Yesterday

Result: Three Sets to Zero

The volleyball league organized by the Shanghai Chinese YMCA Sports Department saw ten heroic teams from Shanghai compete. For six weeks, Haige and Czechoslovakia led the first and second divisions respectively. Yesterday, the two teams met in the finals at the YMCA to determine this year's champion. Qian Yiqin was the referee, and Ling Xitao was the recorder. The match adopted a best-of-five format. As a result, Haige won three straight sets and won the championship.

Czechoslovakia's momentum was strong, initially taking a 6-0 lead. However, they gradually fell behind, though the difference was minimal. If they had been more strategic, Haige would have had difficulty securing victory. However, due to their lack of experience, they lost the first set 18-21.

In the second set, Haige became more flexible. General Cao's attack was invariably successful. However, Czechoslovakia was still able to cope. Unfortunately, in the second half of the set, their formation was disrupted, leading to Haige's pressure, and they failed again. As a result, Haige won again with a score of 21-15.

The third set was a life-or-death battle for both teams. Czechoslovakia's effective response made it difficult for Haige to cope. At one point, they took an 18-15 lead. However, they ultimately failed due to disorganization, which was very regrettable. As a result, Haige won again with a score of 21-18.

The champion team, Haige, was a mix of Fudan University and middle school students. Having fought on the field for a long time, they are famous throughout the Chuansha area. Cao Yanzan and Cheng Mingjue are national volleyball players, and their assistants on the left, right, front, and back are all top-notch. Their victory is a matter of course.

The runner-up team, Czechoslovakia, is the embodiment of the East Asia College of Physical Education. The entire team is well-organized and technically excellent. Their only weakness compared to Haige is their lack of experience.

Three Associations' Swimming Instructor Mr. Yu Binqi 107

Introduces Qian Yi Qin's (Swimming Training Method)

Yu Binqi, swimming instructor of the Shanghai Three Associations Sports Federation, introduces Qian Yiqin's (Swimming Training Method):

Swimming is not only a good way to cool off in the summer and an excellent life-saving technique, but also one of the most beneficial sports, allowing the whole body to develop evenly. Therefore, many people like it. However, there are also many enthusiastic learners, because few Chinese people are skilled in this field, making it difficult for those who study it carefully to find a basis, and even have no way to ask for guidance, and often give up halfway. The Qin Fen Bookstore at No. M117, Huajin Lane, Fourth Malu Road, Shanghai, promotes various sports and spares no effort. To meet the needs of those who study swimming, they have specially invited physical education expert Qian Yiqin to conduct several years of research using scientific methods and write the book (Swimming Training Method), which has now been published. The book is divided into three parts: upper, middle, and lower. The upper part describes the basic exercises of swimming and the methods and secrets of various swimming styles; the middle part is the various diving methods; the lower part is life-saving techniques. There are over 100 illustrations, indicating training methods, which are quite valuable. The whole book is beautifully bound in cloth. (The book is priced at 2.40 yuan, with a special discount of 10%. Please add 10 cents for postage. It is also available at the ticket office of the East Asia College of Physical Education swimming pool in this city.) Anyone who learns to swim will know the training methods by reading this book and can learn on their own without a teacher. This is specially introduced for promotion.

Local News

Government Orders Closure of Postal Services Outside the Pass Yesterday 113

The order from Nanjing arrived at the General Post Office at 10:00 AM yesterday, immediately instructing all locations to temporarily suspend postal services in the eastern provinces. The Shanghai Post Office issued a notice not to send any more items via Siberia Railway to Europe, and instead use sea transport, according to the Far East News Agency. The Shanghai Postal Administration received a confidential telegram order from the Ministry of Transportation in Nanjing at 10:00 AM yesterday, stating that postal services in various bureaus in the eastern provinces will be temporarily closed effective immediately. Director Huang Naishu immediately ordered the bureaus in the eastern provinces to cease operations immediately, and all employees should quickly enter the Pass. He also informed postal bureaus in various provinces to notify the public not to send any more letters, packages, or remittances to the eastern provinces. Work at the General Post Office was particularly tense because of this. Although yesterday was Saturday, all employees continued to work until around 7:00 PM. The details are as follows:

Closure Ordered Due to Intolerable Harassment 114

The Ministry of Transportation believes that recently, the Japanese have instigated rebels to plot to seize postal rights in the eastern provinces, which has gradually progressed from planning to concrete action. Recently, employees of various bureaus outside the Pass have been subjected to brutal oppression by Japanese military police and barbaric surveillance and insults by puppet prosecutors. Most recently, there was the forced issuance of pseudo-national postage stamps. Various actions have made it difficult for our various work tasks to proceed, and the lives of the staff have been experiencing extreme insecurity and threats. It is truly intolerable to be harassed any further. Therefore, with the approval of the Executive Yuan yesterday, it was decided to order the temporary closure of postal services in the eastern provinces, ordering the postal bureaus of the three provinces to cease operations immediately and withdraw all employees. The order was issued yesterday morning and arrived at the Shanghai General Post Office at 10:00 AM. Because of some confidential nature, the authorities did not allow the original text to be published.

Withdrawal of Employees and Suspension of Work 115

After receiving the telegram from the Ministry of Transportation, Director Huang of the Postal Administration immediately issued a confidential telegram, ordering employees in the eastern provinces to cease operations immediately and withdraw all personnel into the Pass, and instructed on all contingency arrangements. At the same time, it was telegraphed to postal bureaus in various locations not to receive or send any more letters, packages, or remittances to the eastern provinces.

Shanghai Post Office Issues Notice 116

In order to prevent residents from sending any more postal items, packages, and remittances to various locations in the eastern provinces, the Shanghai Postal Administration posted a notice on the glass window at the entrance at 9:30 PM last night, stating: Notice is hereby given that, as per the order of the Postal Administration, since the postal service in the three eastern provinces has undergone extraordinary changes, it has been attempting to maintain services for the convenience of the public for several months. Now, due to the circumstances, it is forced to temporarily suspend all operations of the postal bureaus in the three provinces. All drafts issued to and from the bureaus in the three provinces should be stopped. The remitting bank should retrieve the original remittance from the issuing bureau. All kinds of postal items and packages sent to various locations in the three eastern provinces will also be suspended from receipt starting from today, etc. This is hereby notified to inform the public. Postal Director Cha Peilin.

Mail to Europe to be Re-routed by Sea 117

After the closure of the postal bureaus in the eastern provinces, mail bound for European countries via the Siberian Railway will be temporarily rerouted by sea. Once the postal bureaus in the eastern provinces return to normal, it will be transported by the original route. The General Post Office has now negotiated various transportation methods with shipping companies.

Pseudo-Delegate Fujiwara as Pseudo-Director 118

Reporters from the Far East News Agency have learned from Japanese sources that, in order to ensure that the puppet state can successfully achieve the goal of seizing postal rights in Manchuria by August 1st, the Japanese government specially sent a postal expert named (Fujiwara) to Manchuria last month to actively make arrangements. The number of skilled postal staff who have been transferred to Manchuria one after another has reached more than 400. Currently, the rebel faction has officially appointed Fujiwara as the Pseudo-Manchukuo Postmaster General, and others have also been given corresponding titles.

Huang Naishu Discusses Handling of the Situation 119

Yesterday, Huang Naishu, director of the Postal Administration, said to reporters from the Far East News Agency who visited him that the government's decision to close the postal service in the eastern provinces was truly a last resort. The Japanese instigated the puppet state to sabotage, obstruct, and threaten us, and their insidious methods can be said to be extremely unscrupulous, causing the lives of our staff in the three provinces to be in danger and making it difficult for them to work. Therefore, today, it has become intolerable, and there is only this decisive measure to take. Before the order was issued, this bureau had been ordered to arrange everything in advance. Therefore, several weeks ago, all important documents on postal affairs in the three provinces were ordered to be transported to a safe area, and all staff were also notified to be prepared to enter the Pass immediately after receiving the order. Therefore, there is no need to worry about other changes after the official order is issued today. There are about 3,000 postal employees in the three provinces. Some of the lower-level employees may not be able to be transferred into the Pass due to local relations and other reasons. However, it is expected that more than 2,500 people can be transferred back. This time, the employees will be transferred to serve in various locations. Those who cannot obtain a position temporarily will be paid their original salary and wait to be transferred back to serve after the eastern provinces are restored to their original state. As for the various losses suffered by domestic and foreign people due to this closure of postal bureaus in the eastern provinces, the responsibility should be borne by the Japanese. The reporter then asked the director whether the Japanese would overstep their authority and take over postal affairs in the Northeast in the future. Huang replied that if the Japanese disregarded international trust and took this decisive step, we would lodge a protest and seek other ways to counter it.

Song Zewen Held an Important Meeting Yesterday 120

Discussing the Northeast Customs Issue

And Will Host a Banquet for Leaders from All Sectors

According to the National News Agency, Minister of Finance Song Zewen arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday from Nanjing aboard the customs patrol ship "Xiaguang". Yesterday morning at nine o'clock, he summoned Commissioner of Customs Zhang Fuyun and others to his residence to discuss the issue of the seizure of the Northeast customs. The meeting adjourned at 10:40 AM. Around 4:00 PM in the afternoon, they returned to Song's residence for further discussions.

Participants in the Meeting Those participating in Song's meeting at 9:00 AM yesterday included, besides Song himself, three Chinese officials, including Commissioner of Customs Zhang Fuyun, and three Westerners, including a certain Director Smith of the Northeast General Customs. A total of seven people were present. The meeting commenced at 9:15 AM and concluded at 10:40 AM. Around 4:00 PM in the afternoon, Zhang Fuyun returned to Song's residence. Shortly thereafter, Deputy Minister of Finance Zhang Shouyong and Inspector General of Customs Frederick Maze also arrived. However, Zhang Fuyun left shortly after entering. When reporters met Zhang in front of Song's residence and inquired about the results of the talks, Zhang remained tight-lipped, only saying that all inquiries should be directed to Minister Song.

Content of the Meeting Yesterday's meeting at Song's residence was held in strict confidence, and none of the participants revealed any details. However, reporters learned from other sources that the content of the meeting concerned the imposition of taxes on all imports and exports after the blockade of the Northeast customs, with the tax collection points to be located in key areas. Therefore, the discussions yesterday likely revolved around this issue.

Song's Mission According to sources close to Song, his mission in coming to Shanghai is primarily to negotiate the blockade of the Northeast customs. However, it is also essential to have thorough discussions with representatives of the local banking and financial sectors regarding military expenditures for bandit suppression and the conversion from taels to yuan. Therefore, Song plans to host a banquet at his residence tonight or tomorrow night to discuss these matters with leaders from the banking and financial sectors. Director of the Currency Department Xu Kan also arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning from Nanjing by train. It is reported that Song will not stay in Shanghai for long this time. After another round of discussions with representatives from the banking and financial sectors, he will return to Nanjing.

Luo Wengan Visited the Courts Yesterday 121

Returned to Nanjing in the Afternoon

Minister of Judicial Administration and concurrently Minister of Foreign Affairs Luo Wengan arrived in Shanghai the night before last from Nanjing. He initially intended to stay at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai office in Fenglinqiao. However, after arriving at the office at 11:00 PM, Luo found the accommodations and meals inconvenient and immediately changed his residence to the Xinxin Hotel on Nanjing Road. Yesterday morning around 8:00 AM, Luo left his residence to visit lawyer Zhang Shizhao. He then proceeded to inspect various levels of courts in Shanghai. At 3:15 PM in the afternoon, he hastily returned to Nanjing.

Inspection of the Courts Luo left his hotel at 8:00 AM yesterday morning for lawyer Zhang Shizhao's residence, where they talked for about an hour and had breakfast. He then accompanied Shanghai District Court President Shen Xiqing to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court in the French Concession for inspection. He was accompanied by Liang Renjie, President of the Second Branch of the High Court, to inspect the Second Special District Court on Xuehuali Road, where he was joined by President Ying of the court and others to observe the civil court trial. At 9:30 AM, he went to the Nanshi District Court for inspection, accompanied by President Shen to observe the handling of cases in various courts. Around 10:00 AM, he went to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court and the First Special District Court for inspection, where he was received by President Shen Jiayi of the Second High Court and observed the trial of cases for about 45 minutes before concluding his visit. He then returned to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai office. After arriving at the office at 11:05 AM, he had lunch with the Director of the Foreign Affairs Office, Yu Ming, and then returned to his residence for a brief rest. At 2:30 PM, he ordered the Railways Bureau to prepare a train for his return to Nanjing. The Railways Bureau prepared a special M2 train. Luo arrived at the station at 2:05 PM and departed for Nanjing at 3:15 PM.

Luo's Remarks A reporter from the Huadong News Agency learned yesterday afternoon that Luo was going to Nanjing and immediately went to the North Station to interview him. By then, Luo had already boarded the train. He said that his visit to Shanghai was solely to inspect the courts in Shanghai and had no other purpose. He had already met with Minister of Finance Song Zewen in Nanjing and therefore did not visit him after arriving in Shanghai. He added that due to urgent diplomatic matters in Nanjing, he could not stay in Shanghai longer and was returning to Nanjing in haste. As the train was about to depart, the reporter shook hands with Luo to bid farewell.

Reason for the Inspection Regarding the reason for Luo's inspection of the courts in Shanghai, a reporter from the Huadong News Agency visited Xiao Jinfang, the chief clerk of the Second Special District Court, and others yesterday. They learned that Luo's inspection was due to the expiration of the agreement to recover the special district courts in the Public Concession and the French Concession on March 31 of next year. At that time, the Ministry of Judicial Administration and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs will need to renegotiate the recovery methods with the relevant authorities. Furthermore, foreigners have frequently obstructed our efforts to recover judicial rights and have often attacked the courts, as evidenced by the recent case of the Russian beggar in the Second Special District Court. Such slanderous rhetoric has significantly impacted our progress in recovering jurisdiction. Therefore, Luo personally came to Shanghai to inspect whether the courts have given cause for criticism. During the inspection yesterday, Luo found the various aspects of the courts to be commendable and expressed his satisfaction.

The City Government Approved the Reduction or Exemption of Land Tax in War Zones 122

Approved by the Municipal Council Meeting

The measures for reducing or exempting land tax in disaster areas have been reviewed and approved by the Municipal Land, Finance, and Social Affairs Bureaus after jointly dispatching personnel to conduct on-site inspections. The results of the discussions, based on the severity of the disaster, were submitted to the Municipal Government for approval, which was approved at the 208th Municipal Council meeting. The measures proposed by the bureaus will be implemented. The document submitted to the Municipal Government is as follows: It is respectfully submitted for a joint response. We received instructions No. 912 and No. 30 from your office, stating that Wu Xuen, the managing director of the Jiangwan District Disaster Relief Association, submitted a petition stating that the district was severely affected by the disaster, requesting relief and exemption from this year's land tax and past arrears. We were instructed to discuss the overall measures and plan comprehensively, and to clearly investigate the severity of the damage and submit a report with suggestions for review. While complying with these instructions, we received another instruction No. 1287 on the 14th of this month, stating that Gu Lügui, chairman of the Shanghai Disaster Area Federation, submitted a petition requesting a reduction in land tax and spring housing tax, and we were instructed to handle it together. We jointly dispatched personnel to various war zones for on-site inspections. We found that Jiangwan District was the center of the Sino-Japanese War, where the two sides confronted each other for more than a month. Houses were reduced to ruins, and villagers were displaced and had nowhere to live. Fertile fields were dug into trenches, and military roads were built. High artillery emplacements and barbed wire fences stretched for dozens of miles, leaving a desolate and miserable scene. The villages near the Paotaiwan area in Wusong District were particularly severely damaged. Houses were bombed, crops were trampled, and all livestock were slaughtered, resulting in significant losses. Yinhang District, bordering Jiangwan and Wusong, had about 70-80% of its villages destroyed by bombing. Poultry and livestock were also slaughtered and eaten. Yinxiang District was the starting point of the war. About dozens of houses in the villages at the end of Daisiwei Road were burned and looted by traitors. As for the other villages, although they appeared to be less damaged on the surface, they were practically deserted. Pengpu District, located between Jiangwan and Zhenru, was less important in terms of its terrain. Four or five villages were destroyed, and agricultural tools and livestock were lost. Zhenru District, bordering Zhabei Dachan, was also a contested area during the war. Artillery emplacements and trenches were everywhere, and the local area was devastated. After careful investigation of the above six districts, Jiangwan and Wusong Districts were the most severely affected, followed by Yinhang and Zhenru, and then Yinxiang and Pengpu. As for the other districts, although they were not directly affected by the war, their indirect losses were also significant. In addition, since the beginning of summer, there have been continuous days of rain, causing the roots of crops to rot, resulting in a sharp decline in wheat production. On the 23rd of this month, our bureau and others discussed the results and decided: (1) All districts in the city should reduce the land tax according to the severity of the disaster. (2) Jiangwan and Wusong Districts were the most severely affected and are proposed to be completely exempt from the full amount of the 21st year's summer tax (including the 20% of the summer silver that was diverted to water disaster relief in the past; this will no longer be diverted in the future). Yinhang and Zhenru Districts were less severely affected and are proposed to reduce the summer tax by 60%. Yinxiang and Pengpu Districts are proposed to reduce the summer tax by 40%. Zhabei District is entirely an urban area with less farmland and is proposed to reduce the summer tax by 30%. (3) For the remaining districts, except for Hunan and Pusong Districts, it is proposed to reduce the summer tax by 20%. (4) The remaining amount of the summer silver in each district is proposed to be postponed to the collection of the winter tax to alleviate the people's difficulties. (5) Regarding the arrears from previous years in each district, it is proposed that they not be exempted, because these arrears do not necessarily belong to the poor. If they are exempted, it would be unfair to those who have already paid, and opening this door will inevitably affect future collections. (6) Regarding the request to exempt housing tax, it has been announced by your office that housing tax in war zones will be exempted for the spring and summer seasons. As for the standards for reducing or exempting housing tax in other districts, opinions have been submitted in the case of reducing or exempting rent, which was reviewed and discussed by this finance bureau in accordance with the instructions. According to the above review, the total amount of land tax reduction is estimated to be more than 172,000 yuan. Due to the previous instructions, the Land Bureau will separately investigate and create a list of the amount of summer silver to be reduced or exempted in each disaster-affected district of the city in the 20th year and submit it in a separate document. We hereby submit the joint review and discussion of the land tax reduction measures for your review and instructions. It is in the public interest. Furthermore, this submission was drafted by the Social Affairs Bureau and jointly submitted without a seal. Respectfully submitted to Mayor Wu, Director of the Land Bureau Jin Liren, Director of the Finance Bureau Cai Zengji, and Director of the Social Affairs Bureau Wu Xingya.

Hu Jinzhong, a Soldier of the Arrested 19th Route Army, Escaped Danger Yesterday 123

Describing the Inhumane Treatment He Suffered

Liang Fang and Two Others Are Still in Critical Condition

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, Liang Guangxin, a first-class private in the Special Service Battalion of the 78th Division of the 19th Route Army, Fang Da, a second-class private in the Second Company of the Second Regiment of the 155th Brigade, and Hu Jinzhong, a soldier of the 156th Brigade, were arrested by the Japanese army at the Osaka Wharf on the afternoon of the 19th. Hu Jinzhong escaped danger the night before last. According to Wu, the details of his escape are as follows:

Arrested Details Hu Jinzhong, Fang Da, Liang Guangxin, and other soldiers of the 19th Route Army, after recovering from injuries sustained during the Anti-Japanese War at the Bengbu Military Hospital, took a Jinpu train to the capital on the 15th, transferred to the Jinghu train, and arrived in Shanghai on the 17th. They were preparing to take a Dada Wharf steamer to Fujian to rejoin their unit. They stayed at a small inn at the Jinliyuan Wharf. On the afternoon of the 19th, they hired rickshaws and told the drivers to take them to the Dada Wharf, but the drivers mistakenly heard Osaka Wharf. They were seen by Japanese Marines guarding the wharf. Because they were wearing military uniforms with the 19th Route Army insignia, they were immediately arrested without explanation and beaten with rifle butts, causing injuries all over their bodies. They were then imprisoned in a large oil drum by the Huangpu River at the Osaka Wharf, guarded by Indian police and Japanese soldiers in charge of the wharf. They were not given food or drink, and were subjected to all kinds of harsh treatment, which was inhumane.

Escape Details Hu Jinzhong is from Hengzhou, Hunan, and is 16 years old. He was less severely injured. Fang Da was the most seriously injured, with his left arm broken. Liang Guangxin was unable to move due to his injuries and his life was

Page 14

was in critical danger. They were sure to suffocate or starve to death in the drum. On the night of the 22nd, Hu Jinzhong saw that the Indian police in charge of the wharf were far away, and the Japanese Marines guarding them were all drunk. He seized the opportunity to climb out and fled to the tram company factory in the Public Concession on Yangshupu Road. At dawn, he was seen by workers who, after hearing the details of his arrest and abuse by the Japanese army, pleaded for rescue and transfer to the Public Security Bureau.

Escorted to the Bureau A coppersmith at the tram company reported to the Chinese employees of the company. After questioning him in detail, fearing that he would be discovered by the Japanese army, they took off Hu Jinzhong's military uniform and insignia and gave him a set of student clothes to disguise himself. The workers gave him food and drink. Yesterday morning at 8:00 AM, a Chinese employee took him by car to the Fifth District Police Station in Zhabei and gave him four silver dollars. District Chief He Yiming inquired in detail about his arrest and abuse. Because the matter concerned the Japanese army detaining and insulting our soldiers, which was a serious matter, he prepared a document and sent police to protect him and take him by car to the Public Security Bureau headquarters at 10:30 AM yesterday morning.

Temporary Residence at the Bureau Public Security Bureau Chief Wen Yingxing, after receiving a report that Fang Da and other soldiers of the 19th Route Army were detained and insulted by the Japanese army, was secretly investigating the matter. Yesterday, after receiving a report from the Fifth District, he sent Section Chief Wang Zhijing of the Second Section to question him in detail. It was reported that he also sent Hong Qi, the director of the Foreign Affairs Division, to accompany the escaped soldier Hu Jinzhong to the Japanese Consulate at 1:00 PM to investigate the truth. The Japanese Consul shirked responsibility, claiming that the matter was under the jurisdiction of the Marines and only agreed to send personnel to question the Marines. At the same time, the Public Security Bureau reported the details of Hu Jinzhong's escape to the Municipal Government. Currently, Hu Jinzhong is temporarily residing at the Public Security Bureau headquarters.

The Noulens Requested a Transfer of Jurisdiction Again 124

Requesting That the Shanghai High Court Branch Hear the Case

The Noulens previously petitioned the Supreme Court to transfer jurisdiction to the Shanghai-Jiangsu High Court Branch, but the petition was rejected. Yesterday, their attorney submitted another petition. The original petition is as follows: Regarding the continued request for a transfer of jurisdiction, the issue of jurisdiction in this case has raised doubts. After submitting a petition to your court requesting a transfer, it has now been rejected, stating that the original petition's claims are purely objections to jurisdiction and do not explain whether the original trial court has the circumstances listed in Article 21 of the Criminal Procedure Law, so it is difficult to consider it reasonable. Although this ruling cannot be appealed according to law, there is no limit to the number of requests for a transfer of jurisdiction. Even after a rejection, if it is still believed that there are circumstances under Article 21 of the Criminal Procedure Law, it is permissible to continue the request (see the explanation of Article 415 of the Criminal Procedure Collection). The reasons for the continued request for a transfer of jurisdiction are stated as follows: (1) All legal provisions have both a principle and an exception. The so-called principle is the provision that must be applied as a matter of course and is not allowed to be changed without reason. The so-called exception is a temporary remedy adopted when the provisions of the principle cannot be applied in fact due to special reasons. Therefore, in applying the law, the provisions of the principle should be absolutely observed. Only when the provisions of the principle are impossible to apply in fact, it is not allowed to abuse the exception and distort the meaning. One is an absolute and obvious definition, while the other is a relative and accidental variation. (2) The only legal court of first instance in this case, according to Article 13 of the Criminal Procedure Law and Article 1 of the Implementation Regulations for the Punishment of Crimes Endangering the Republic of China, should obviously belong to the Shanghai High Court Branch. The Jiangsu High Court had no jurisdiction from the beginning. Later, due to the transition of military institutions, it was repeatedly transformed. The Ministry of Judicial Administration, through administrative procedures, did not return the case to the Shanghai High Court Branch of original jurisdiction, but arbitrarily ordered it to be handed over to the Jiangsu High Court for jurisdiction (see the last line of page 2 of the indictment). Even if there are slight reasons to justify this, it must be recognized as an exceptional variation, not as it should be in principle. There is no doubt that the petitioner's request to transfer the case from an exceptional and illegal court to a court of principle and legality is for the sake of absolute respect for Chinese law and has no other effect. If the petitioners are guilty, the Shanghai High Court Branch will also be able to enforce the law and will never let them go unpunished. How could it damage the dignity of Chinese justice? Now, the court with original jurisdiction firmly insists that it has no jurisdiction, while the court with no jurisdiction from the beginning insists that it has jurisdiction. Furthermore, it fails to explain why the Shanghai High Court Branch has no jurisdiction and whether there are reasons under Article 21 of the Criminal Procedure Law if it has jurisdiction. This is enough to cause suspicion. Moreover, the trial is held in Nanjing, which is not only inconvenient for the petitioners but also not convenient for the court's staff. There is also no explicit basis in the Criminal Procedure Law and the Court Organization Law. This is what the petitioners are greatly confused about. (3) Since the provisions of Article 21 of the Criminal Procedure Law are an exceptional remedy, if the Shanghai High Court Branch found that the special circumstances listed in that article made it impossible to apply Article 13 and Article 1 of the Implementation Regulations for the Punishment of Crimes Endangering the Republic of China, which are prescribed in principle, the branch would have automatically requested your court to designate a transfer, without waiting for the request of a military institution. The parties in this case would have also requested a transfer long ago. Not only do the parties absolutely recognize the branch as the only legal court to accept the case and have never raised any objections, but the branch itself has never indicated that it has any reason to be without jurisdiction. There has also been no ruling from your court designating a transfer. The transfer was only approved due to the request of a military institution. After the military institution recognized that it had no jurisdiction, it should have been returned to the Shanghai High Court Branch of original jurisdiction for continued acceptance. This is undoubtedly obvious in theory. However, instead of returning it to the original trial court, it was transferred to the Ministry of Judicial Administration. The procedure was extremely wrong, as the Ministry of Judicial Administration is not an agency for accepting litigation cases. Unexpectedly, the Ministry of Judicial Administration not only did not refuse to accept it and order its return to the original trial court, but ordered it to be handed over to the Jiangsu High Court, which was not the original trial court, after accepting it. Is this not one mistake after another? The Shanghai High Court Branch, because the Ministry of Judicial Administration is its superior administrative agency, was unable to protest. The Jiangsu High Court Branch also believed that it was an order from a superior administrative agency and was unable to refuse. They tolerated each other, and a great mistake was made. If the Ministry of Judicial Administration had been able to order the Shanghai High Court Branch of original jurisdiction to continue accepting the case in accordance with the law, the petitioners are confident that the branch would have had no objections. (4) Looking at the overall situation, all requests that are beneficial to the petitioners are strictly interpreted according to the provisions, fault-finding, and are rejected. The language is righteous and the words are strict, and no consideration is given at all (for example, the petitioners' defense attorney, in order to verify the handwriting on the evidence, requested permission to take photographs, but the request was rejected, stating that there was no legal basis. However, Article 175 of the Criminal Procedure Law stipulates that the defense attorney may inspect the case files and evidence objects and may copy the case files. The method of copying may be with a brush, pen, pencil, copying, or photography, and there is no strict restriction. Moreover, it is necessary to photograph in order to carefully review the handwriting, except for the original. Under these circumstances, the judge, for the sake of the parties' interests, may use his discretion to allow it. However, because the word "photography" is not explicitly mentioned in the law, it is said that there is no legal basis. The petitioners truly do not know why this case, which should be kept secret before the investigation, has all the evidence photographed and published in Chinese and Western newspapers for widespread publicity. Furthermore, it is not known in which law it is stipulated that evidence can be photographed and published in newspapers before the investigation.) All matters that are unfavorable to the petitioners, on the other hand, are not spared from violating the provisions of the principle, but instead distorting the provisions of the exception to accommodate them, and even sometimes there is no basis for the exception (such as borrowing the Nanjing court). The reason for this is nothing more than that Nanjing is the political center. Under the influence of this political power, there are all kinds of conveniences to directly control the judiciary, to surround the judiciary with the political environment, and to lose the independent spirit of free exercise. Under these special circumstances, can the petitioners still expect a fair trial? This is the petitioners' distress that they have to continue to request that the Shanghai High Court Branch continue to accept the case. (5) In principle, the Shanghai High Court Branch should have jurisdiction over the first instance in this case. Since there are no circumstances under Article 21 of the Criminal Procedure Law, there is no basis for a transfer. As for the interpretation of the four words "original trial court," your court now distorts them from a changing standpoint and refers to the Jiangsu High Court. However, the petitioners always refer to the Shanghai High Court Branch from the original standpoint. Therefore, although the current request is for a transfer of jurisdiction in name, it is actually only a request to restore the original state and return the case to the Shanghai High Court Branch for continued acceptance. In short, this case is of great importance. The petitioners do not reject the trial of a legal court, but believe that the court should consider the law and the interests of the petitioners in every way. They certainly do not want it to violate the principles of the law, distort the provisions of the exception, or even have no provisions to cite, only to deliberately inflict great harm on the petitioners and deprive them of the rights they should enjoy according to the law in order to accommodate the government. It has been like this in the past, and it can be known in the future. However, the petitioners still hope that the court will not damage its own solemn and sacred spirit, its own bright and upright attitude, and its own weaknesses of compromising and catering to the world because of the petitioners. To further explain that the circumstances stated in Article 21 of the Criminal Procedure Law do indeed have the risk of unfairness, they continue to request your court to approve the transfer of the current illegal jurisdiction and return it to the Shanghai High Court Branch for continued acceptance in accordance with Article 22 of the same law with the spirit of utmost fairness. Respectfully submitted to the Supreme Court, July 23, 21st year of the Republic of China, by the petitioners Noulens and Wang Deli, attorneys Chen Ying and Pei Si.

However, the Chinese judicial authorities believe that regardless of whether they are real or fake, they will still be tried according to the law and will not change their position in the slightest because of

character.

Wang Xiaolai delivered a welcoming speech, followed by the three representatives reporting on their experiences. They stated that their trip was very positive, and the people of Hong Kong and Guangdong showed warm sympathy and deep hope for the abolition of civil war. They believed that with concerted efforts and unwavering determination, success would eventually be achieved. The reports of the three representatives are summarized below:

Zhu Qinglan's report on the consultations: Upon arriving in Hong Kong on the 11th, they were warmly welcomed by various organizations and the public. After landing, they separately visited key military and political figures such as Tang Shaochuan, Li Zongren, Chen Jitang, Lin Yunga, Xiao Focheng, and Lin Yizhong, as well as leaders of local public organizations, explaining the mission of their trip. At 11 AM, they attended a welcome meeting at the Guangzhou Lingnan Club. At noon, they attended a banquet hosted by Chen Jitang. At 6 PM, they attended a banquet hosted by Li Zongren. At 7 PM, they attended a welcome meeting hosted by the Silver Industry Association. At 8 PM, they gave a speech at the YMCA. At 12 AM, they returned to the Asia Hotel and met with student representatives. All speeches and remarks made at the various gatherings focused on the abolition of civil war as the only way to unite against foreign aggression. During the banquet hosted by Chen Jitang, all senior military and political figures were present. They were open and frank, expressing their views without reservation. Chen first explained the situation in Guangdong and then inquired whether the Abolish the Civil War Alliance had any political background. After the representatives explained that the abolition of civil war was a purely patriotic movement aimed at uniting against foreign aggression and had no political purpose, the authorities expressed their understanding. The Guangzhou Chamber of Commerce is now leading the Abolish the Civil War Alliance in Guangzhou. With their mission completed, the representatives took a ship from Guangzhou to Foshan on the 16th and then returned to Shanghai via Macau. In conclusion, the trip gave the representatives the feeling that the abolition of civil war movement, if carried out with determination and unity by the entire nation, with purity and effort, would surely achieve good results.

Chen Liting's Explanation of Civil War: Representative Chen Liting explained the meaning of "civil war" at the banquet hosted by Chen Jitang, stating that the establishment of the Abolish the Civil War Alliance stemmed from the patriotic aspirations of the four major commercial organizations in Shanghai. They firmly believed that during this time of national crisis, stopping civil war and uniting together was essential to save the perilous situation and strengthen the country. Otherwise, the nation would be doomed. The alliance was not being used by anyone or acting as a military background for anyone, nor was it a tool for anyone's personal gain. In simple terms, "civil war" referred to any act of possessing troops for self-defense, harming the country and the people, prioritizing personal interests over the well-being of the people, and dividing territories, thereby causing civil war. However, suppressing bandits and communists was the responsibility of the military and political authorities and should not be considered civil war. The judgment of this type of discussion should be sought from public opinion. The alliance has decided to convene a representative assembly in Shanghai to discuss concrete explanations and measures in detail. This is the explanation of "civil war."

Zha Liangzhao's Report on Public Enthusiasm: Representative Zha Liangzhao reported that the warm welcome from the people in Hong Kong, Guangdong, and Macau was deeply moving. It showed that the abolition of civil war was the unanimous desire of the entire nation. Banners reading "Welcome Peace Envoys" were displayed at the piers, and large firecrackers were set off. Hong Kong newspapers published news of the representatives' trip to Guangdong with large headlines covering multiple pages and editorials expressing their hopes. Detailed accounts were given of the trips from Hong Kong to Guangdong and back to Hong Kong. After returning to Hong Kong, at the urging of overseas Chinese in Macau, they took the Zhongxing ship to Macau on the 17th. The warm welcome in Macau was no less enthusiastic than in Hong Kong. All shops displayed national flags. Upon arrival, representatives from the Chamber of Commerce, the Education Association, and other organizations, along with overseas Chinese, gathered at the pier to welcome them. A welcome meeting was held at the Chamber of Commerce. Chairman Fan Jieming delivered a welcoming speech, stating that the abolition of civil war had long been supported by the people, and overseas Chinese were eager to follow and contribute to its implementation. Mr. Zhu responded on behalf of the group, stating that foreign aggression was becoming increasingly urgent, and the Northeast and Shanghai had suffered greatly from the war. Commerce had plummeted, and the people felt that they could not survive unless they stopped the civil war and united against foreign aggression. Therefore, the four organizations in Shanghai initiated the Abolish the Civil War Alliance, which now had 494 participating organizations. He hoped that compatriots at home and abroad would work together to achieve the goal of internal stability and resistance to foreign aggression. After completing their consultations in Macau, they returned to Hong Kong and took the President Hoover ship back to Shanghai on the 19th.

Local News Two

Japanese Soldiers' Vehicle Hits Chinese Person, Attempts to Transport the Injured Elsewhere 130

Two Western Police Officers Perform Their Duty to Provide Assistance

A Certain Western Woman Righteously Argues

Zhu Ashun, a 64-year-old resident of Pudong, runs a milk shed and sells cattle in Yangjiadu, Pudong, earning a good income. Zhu has a sworn friend named Xiang Gou, who runs the Shunxingyuan hot water stall at the intersection of Miller Road and Hankow Road in Hongkou. He has considerable influence in the Hongkou area. Cattle entering and leaving the surrounding villages must go through his hands, or else troubles will inevitably arise later. However, he is a generous and chivalrous man, so people enjoy associating with him. Yesterday morning, Zhu led a calf from Pudong to Xiang Gou's place and sold it for 11 silver dollars. Because of their long-standing friendship, Xiang Gou invited him to lunch before returning. However, Zhu insisted on declining because he was anxious to cross back to Pudong. When he was passing the Xiaocaichang intersection of Miller Road and Wenjianshi Road, a Japanese naval military vehicle suddenly sped by. Zhu was unable to avoid it in time and was knocked to the ground, suffering a severe head injury. The Japanese soldiers in the vehicle, seeing the accident they had caused, immediately jumped out, and two Japanese soldiers carried the injured person onto the vehicle, intending to transport him elsewhere and leave him for dead. Although a police officer on duty witnessed everything, he was too timid to step forward and perform his duty. Two Western police officers happened to be patrolling nearby, and a Chinese police officer reported the details. Seeing that the vehicle had not gone far, the two Western police officers quickly gave chase and negotiated with the Japanese soldiers. As a result, they escorted the vehicle to the entrance of the Tongren Hospital. When the two Western police officers contacted the hospital, the hospital sent a head nurse, a certain Western woman, leading two staff members, and they pushed a stretcher to the side of the road, intending to transfer Zhu Ashun to the stretcher. However, the Japanese soldiers in the vehicle firmly refused to let the injured person down. The Western woman argued strongly and, together with the staff members, forcibly dragged the injured person onto the stretcher. The military vehicle then drove north. The Japanese's hostility towards the Chinese people is evident here.

The Murder of Wen Ying 131

Fan Hongsheng Still Attempts to Frame Others

Will Be Tried Together with Diaoyukeke

After the murder of the female physiognomist Wang Wenying, her teacher, the male physiognomist Diaoyukeke (Cheng Meixian), was suspected of being heavily involved. The police arrested Cheng and took him to the First Special Court for interrogation and detention, as reported in this newspaper. The main culprit, Fan Hongsheng (also known as Fan Ruibao, a 24-year-old from Nanjing), escaped. Although the police were actively pursuing him, he was still not captured. Yesterday morning, old ward police officer You Agen, Su Changsheng, and patrol officer Zhou Guisheng arrested Fan's mother, Mrs. Chen, at No. 1837 Peng Road. Under questioning, they learned that her son Hongsheng was hiding at his sister's residence at No. 965 Jiaotong Road, Zhabei. Officer You and others, together with officers from the Fourth District Public Security Bureau, rushed to the address and arrested him. They found 70 silver dollars and a train timetable (cut from a newspaper) in his pocket. They immediately took him back to the police station. At that time, Fan's nerves seemed to be slightly disturbed.

He loudly sang the "July 7th Small Tune", involving Wenying and himself in the tune. He was then taken into custody, and Mrs. Fan Chen was released. Yesterday morning, the police escorted Fan to the First Criminal Court of the First Special Court, where he was interrogated by Criminal Judge Qian Hongye. Fan Hongsheng hired lawyer Jiang Baoli as his defense counsel. First, police lawyer Ru Baoyi presented the case (previously reported, omitted) and stated that in addition to

Wang Wenying's murder, Wang's mother, Mrs. Wu, was also injured. Therefore, the police filed a public prosecution in accordance with Article 284, Paragraph 1 of premeditated murder and Paragraph 3 of attempted crime. Furthermore, the defendant was previously sentenced to two months' imprisonment by the court on April 28 of last year for

consuming opium and was released on July 7. However, this case also involves Cheng Meixian, who has already been interrogated once by the court and rescheduled to the 27th of this month. Therefore, this case should also be rescheduled and tried together with Cheng Meixian. Subsequently, Officer You submitted a report on the arrest of the defendant, and Chen Ajin testified that she was a servant in Wenying's household and that the defendant did not come often, only once the day before the incident. He came again that

morning and again in the afternoon. Seeing me in the room, he ordered me to buy cigarettes with a two-corner coin. However, the coin was made of lead, so I returned home to exchange it. Then

Miss fell to the ground and died. At that time, only Fan was in the room with Miss and her mother. I was not at the scene when the incident occurred. In addition, Pan Changfu, the coachman of Wenying's second landlord Yang Zhiyi, testified that after the incident, he saw Wang Wu chase after the defendant and that he also helped chase after him, but they suddenly disappeared in Daqing Lane. Subsequently, Fan Hongsheng's mother, Mrs. Fan Chen, testified that the 70 silver dollars found on the defendant were given to him by his sister to buy clothes because he had completely torn all his clothes. The court then ordered that the confiscated 70 silver dollars be returned to Mrs. Fan Chen. When questioned, Fan Hongsheng confessed that he had known Wang Wenying for

a month and that no one had introduced them. That day, I went with another person named Cheng Wenqin, not Cheng Meisheng. The murder was committed by two people together. When escaping, I went out the front door, and he went out the back door. Police lawyer Ru immediately stated that the Cheng Wenqin mentioned by the defendant had been investigated by the police and found to be working with the defendant at the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway Station. Because they had a grudge, he falsely accused him. In reality, there was no relationship. The court then questioned Fan about whether he had previously been sentenced to two months' imprisonment for smoking opium. Fan replied yes. Ru Lawyer immediately requested the court's attention, saying that Fan was still

matter, it can be seen that his brain is still . The court should ask the clerk to record it in the minutes. Judge Qian then ordered the defendant to be taken into custody. This case will be rescheduled for further hearing.

Hong Pinxuan Forcibly Divorces 132

Falsely Claims Mother-in-Law is Ill and Comes to Shanghai

Privately Asks Hotel and Pier to Abandon

Shi Cuiying, a woman from Zhoushan, 21 years old, married Hong Pinxuan, a native of Ningbo, through a matchmaker in March last year. After getting married, they lived together in the Wang Guxing clothing store, Huacui , Ti'ao Bridge, Hongkou, North Shanghai. This year, Hong, for some unknown reason, treated Cuiying like a thorn in his side. If she slightly disobeyed him, she would be beaten. On the 17th of this month, Cuiying's mother, Shi Hu, suddenly received a letter from her son-in-law, Hong Pinxuan, in her hometown, saying that Cuiying was seriously ill and asking her to come to Shanghai immediately. Ms. Shi took a ship on the 21st and rushed to Hong's house. Cuiying was surprised to see her and asked why she had come to Shanghai in such hot weather. Ms. Shi told her everything, and Cuiying realized that someone must be playing a prank. However, she did not investigate further. Until about 3 PM the day before yesterday, Hong suddenly invited Ms. Shi to visit a hotel. Ms. Shi did not suspect anything and followed him. After arriving at a certain room in the hotel, not long after sitting down, several of Hong's friends suddenly broke into the room. At Hong's greeting, they took out a divorce agreement and said sternly to Ms. Shi, "Now, I and Cuiying have disagreements, so I want to end the relationship. I will marry another wife later, and Cuiying must not interfere. If she marries another man, she must compensate me for a loss of 200 yuan." "The divorce agreement is already here, but I am afraid there are no witnesses, so I falsely claimed that Cuiying was seriously ill and specially sent a letter urging you to come to Shanghai and invited so many friends. Please sign this divorce agreement now, otherwise, I will send you to your death immediately." Ms. Shi initially said to Hong, "Why is my daughter not good? If you want to divorce her, I cannot sign it casually now." However, after being repeatedly threatened by Hong and others, Ms. Shi, being ignorant and fearful, signed the agreement. That night, she was placed under house arrest in the room. After Cuiying was separated from her mother, she did not see her return. Later, Hong returned home, and Cuiying immediately asked about her mother's whereabouts. He said, "Because she was playing around and was tired, she is sleeping in the hotel. She is going back to her hometown tomorrow. I told you to go to the pier to see her off." Cuiying asked again, "Since my mother is going back to her hometown, why doesn't she come here for a while?" Hong said, "I really don't know." After one night, Hong called Cuiying to the pier yesterday to see her off. He called together many friends and used a car to send Cuiying to the Dada Pier in Nanshi. Cuiying did not see her mother and became suspicious. Hong changed his words and said, "I will go pick up your mother." Not long after, her mother did come. Hong then changed his expression and said to Cuiying, "Now your mother has already written the divorce agreement for us. From now on, we will go our separate ways." After saying that, he left. Cuiying was stunned after hearing this and explained what had happened the night before. Cuiying was greatly angered by Hong's treachery and shouted again and again, and immediately wanted to commit suicide by throwing herself into the river. Her mother immediately hugged her and cried, "Do you want to die? Okay, I will come with you." At that time, a police officer from the First District Police Station heard about it and rushed to pull them apart and took them back to the district. During the preliminary hearing, the mother and daughter explained what happened. As the matter concerned a marital dispute, they were instructed to prepare a document and send it to the bureau for review.

The Work of the Chinese Representative Office of the Investigation Team 135

Jin Wensi's Conversation Before Going North

Mr. Jin Wensi of the Chinese Representative Office of the League of Nations Investigation Team came to Shanghai at the beginning of the month. Now that the investigation team has returned to China from Japan, Mr. Jin was urged by Mr. Gu to go north by telegram. He took the Swatow wheel of Taikoo Company with his wife and two sons yesterday morning (23rd). This newspaper reporter visited Mr. Jin on the boat and asked about the work of the representative office in the past and in the future. I was informed of the respective answers below. Mr. Jin said, in addition to reception and general affairs, the most important part of the representative office's work is the preparation and translation of the statement of argument, as well as the meeting with the investigation team and the discussion and research of specialized issues. Regarding the part of the statement of argument, two cases were submitted in April, one is a general statement of argument, which summarizes China's position on the Sino-Japanese dispute, and the other is a statement of argument on the issue of parallel lines in the South Manchuria Road, but at that time the investigation team was going to Beijing and Hankou under the leadership of Shanghai. After arriving in Ping, the pseudo-country put forward the problem of refusing Gu, and the group tried to deal with it with Japan, and then went to the Eastern Province for on-site investigation, and Representative Gu accompanied them everywhere from Shanghai to the Eastern Province, so there was no time to take care of the preparation of other statements of argument. Before leaving the customs, Representative Gu assigned the various statements of argument to be submitted to the various commissioners for drafting, and the drafting of each commissioner took more than a month. After the investigation team returned to Ping in early June, Representative Gu carefully reviewed each statement of argument and submitted them to the group separately. This statement of argument can be roughly divided into three categories: (1) Regarding the situation of Japan's aggression, all the circumstances of the Eastern Incident this time, the circumstances of the Japanese army in places outside the Eastern Province seeking trouble, the massacre of overseas Chinese in Korea and the Wanbaoshan case, and other political and economic aggressions are included. (2) Regarding the legal position, in addition to detailing in the general statement of argument how Japan violated the Covenant of the League of Nations, the Non-War Convention, the Nine-Power Treaty, and international law, regarding the four-article treaty generated by Article 21, according to the advocacy of our country in the two meetings of the Paris-Washington Conference, especially according to the legal effect of the parliament's denial of the treaty, it is advocated to amend and abolish the issue of parallel lines. We declare that our country has no obligation not to build parallel lines in the treaty. For the issue of the South Manchuria Road Patrol, we declare how Japan violated the treaty and did not withdraw the patrol, which led to today's disaster. In addition, there are other legal issues, which will not be detailed here. (3) Regarding refuting Japan's attack, for example, the answer to the 53 outstanding cases claimed by Japan, the clarification of the anti-foreign remarks in our country's textbooks pointed out by Japan, the explanation of the Fengpiao issue, the explanation of the boycott of Japanese goods issue, and the claim made by Japan that the development of the Eastern Province is entirely due to Japan's efforts, it lists the facts of China's construction achievements in the Eastern Province to prove the unreliability of Japan's statement. All such issues are included. Mr. Jin also said that in addition to the various documents that have been submitted, there are still some that have not been submitted, and they are being rushed to prepare. In addition, the problems raised by the commissioners of the investigation team are also quite a few. The commissioners of our side also study and reply to this problem in order, or hold meetings with the commissioners of the group from time to time to discuss. As for the return to Ping of the investigation team, the committees will also hold meetings with our country's representatives from time to time to discuss various issues. In general, the work of our country's representative office can only be concluded after the investigation team's report is completed. However, for the sake of saving time at that time, these twenty or thirty kinds of statements of argument were drafted in Western languages, and all of them must be translated into Chinese. In addition, in addition to reporting to the government at any time, the representative office must also submit a general report. This kind of work also takes a lot of time, and it will take about two months to complete.
